107 // temporary workspace buffer for FFT implementations
109 static float* gTempBufferPtr = 0;
110 
112 // current buffer length for above pointer
114 static int32 gTempBufferSize = 0;
115 
117 // table of pre-calculated sin & cos values for use by ping pong FFT
119 static float* gSinCosTablePtr = 0;
120 
122 // length of currently allocated sin & cos table
124 static int32 gSinCosTableSize = 0;
125 
127 //
128 // log2max
129 //
130 // This function computes the ceiling of log2(n). For example:
131 //
132 // log2max(7) = 3
133 // log2max(8) = 3
134 // log2max(9) = 4
135 //
137 static int32 log2max(int32 n)
138 {
139  int32 power = 1;
140  int32 k = 1;
141 
142  if (n==1) {
143  return 0;
144  }
145 
146  while ((k <<= 1) < n) {
147  power++;
148  }
149 
150  return power;
151 }

153 
155 //
156 // EnsureStaticBufferSize
157 //
158 // This function is used to ensure that the global pointer gTempBufferPtr
159 // is large enough to hold complexCount complex floats. It compares the
160 // currently allocated length (if there is one) with the desired length,
161 // and, if necessary, allocates a new, larger pointer.
162 // It will NOT shrink the pointer, because a function higher in the calling
163 // chain may need the larger size.
165 static int EnsureStaticBufferSize(int32 complexCount)
166 {
167  int32 result = 0;
168 
169  if (gTempBufferSize < complexCount) {
170  gTempBufferSize = complexCount;
171 
172  if (gTempBufferPtr) {
173  free(gTempBufferPtr);
174  gTempBufferPtr = 0;
175  }
176 
177  gTempBufferPtr = (float*) valloc(2*complexCount*sizeof(float));
178 
179  if (!gTempBufferPtr) result = ENOMEM;
180  if (result != 0) {
181  gTempBufferPtr = 0;
182  gTempBufferSize = 0;
183  }
184  }
185 
186  return result;
187 }

191 // InitFFTSinCos
192 // Initialize cos & sin lookup table.
194 static int InitFFTSinCos(int32 len) {
195  int32 result = 0;
196  int32 i;
197  float angle;
198  float *sinCosTable;
199  float curSin;
200  float curCos;
201  int32 pointerSize;
202 
204  // set length indicator to new length
206  gSinCosTableSize = len;
207 
209  // deallocate old pointer if there is one
211  if(gSinCosTablePtr) free(gSinCosTablePtr);
212 
214  // calculate appropriate pointer size for table. Ensure a minimum length for
215  // a one-entry (two-value: cos & sin) table
217  pointerSize = sizeof(float) * len;
218 
219  if (!pointerSize) pointerSize = 2 * sizeof(float);
220 
222  // alloc new pointer for sin & cos table
224  gSinCosTablePtr = (float*) valloc(pointerSize);
225 
226  if (!gSinCosTablePtr) result = ENOMEM;
227 
228  if (result == 0) {
230  // get pointer to start of sin cos table
231  // to reference as array
233  sinCosTable = (float*)gSinCosTablePtr;
234 
235  if (len < 4) {
237  // always create first entries in table
239  sinCosTable[0] = 1;
240  sinCosTable[1] = 0;
241 
243  // if len is 2, then add second pair to table
245  if (len == 2) {
246  sinCosTable[2] = -1;
247  sinCosTable[3] = 0;
248  }
249  } else {
251  // calculate cos & sin for range of
252  // [0, pi].
254  for(i=0; i < len/4; i++) {
255  angle = 2.0 * PI * i/len;
256 
257  curCos = cos(angle);
258  curSin = sin(angle);
259 
260  sinCosTable[2*i] = curCos;
261  sinCosTable[2*i+1] = curSin;
262 
263  sinCosTable[len/2 + 2*i] = -curSin;
264  sinCosTable[len/2 + 2*i + 1] = curCos;
265  }
266  }
267  }
268 
270  // if there was an error, then dealloc
271  // anything we allocated, and reset
272  // length indicator to zero.
274  if (result != 0) {
275  if (gSinCosTablePtr != 0) {
276  free(gSinCosTablePtr);
277  gSinCosTablePtr = 0;
278  }
279 
280  gSinCosTableSize = 0;
281  }
282 
283  return result;
284 
285 }

289 // ShutdownFFT
290 //
291 // deallocates any memory curently allocated for fft buffers.
293 void ShutdownFFT()
294 {
295  if (gSinCosTablePtr != 0) {
296  free(gSinCosTablePtr);
297  gSinCosTablePtr = 0;
298  }
299 
300  gSinCosTableSize = 0;
301 
302  if (gTempBufferPtr != 0) {
303  free(gTempBufferPtr);
304  gTempBufferPtr = 0;
305  }
306 
307  gTempBufferSize = 0;
308 }

314 // scalar implementation of altivec forward real fft above
316 static int32 fft_real_forward_scalar(float *data, int32 len)
317 {
318  int32 result = 0;
319  double updateA, updateB;
320 
321  double currentCos, currentSin, tempCos1;
322 
323  float realLo, realHi, imLo, imHi;
324 
325  float realResultLo, realResultHi, imResultLo, imResultHi;
326 
327  float realDiff, imDiff, realSum, imSum;
328 
329  float *pInLo, *pInHi;
330 
331  int32 i;
332 
334  // for length of 0 or 1 we do nothing
336  if (len < 2) return 0;
337 
339  // perform a forward complex fft on our
340  // real signal data, treating it as a
341  // half-length complex signal.
343  result = FFTComplex(data, len/2, -1);
344 
345  if (result == 0) {
347  //
348  // Given c = cos(w) and s = sin(w), if we
349  // want to find the cos and sin of w plus
350  // some small angle d, then we can do so
351  // by defining:
352  //
353  // a = 2 * ((sin(d/2)) ^ 2)
354  // b = sin(d)
355  //
356  // Then, we can calculate the cos and sin
357  // of the updated angle w+d as:
358  //
359  // cos(w+d) = c - ac - bs
360  // sin(w+d) = s - as + bc
361  //
362  // We will need to incrementally calculate
363  // cos(w) and sin(w), so we define the
364  // following scalar values. We use scalar
365  // because we need the precision of doubles,
366  // and vectors are floats.
367  //
369 
370  updateA = sin(PI/len);
371  updateB = sin(2*PI/len);
372  updateA *= updateA*2;
373 
375  // start with sin(0) and cos(0)
377 
378  currentCos = 1;
379  currentSin = 0;
380 
382  // first, calculate re[0], and re[n/2]. we don't bother to do the
383  // sin, cos multiplies, because we know that they are zero and one.
385 
386  realResultLo = data[0]+data[1];
387  realResultHi = data[0]-data[1];
388 
390  // store re[0]. We don't calculate im[0] because we know that it is 0.
392  data[0] = realResultLo;
393 
395  // store re[n/2]. We don't calculate im[n/2] because we know it
396  // is 0. We store re[n/2] in the position of im[0] because we
397  // don't want to take up any more space than the source data, and
398  // if we were to store it in the n/2 position, it would be past
399  // the array of source data, which ranges from 0 to (n/2)-1.
401  data[1] = realResultHi;
402 
404  // Start our source pointers to point at re[1] and re[(n/2)-1].
406  pInLo = &data[2];
407  pInHi = &data[len-2];
408 
410  // for each loop iteration, we calculate two complex results (four
411  // floats), so we iterate through the loop len/4 times
413  for (i = 0; i < len/4; i++) {
415  // calculate the new sin and cos values
417 
418  tempCos1 = currentCos - (updateA*currentCos + updateB * currentSin);
419  currentSin = currentSin - (updateA*currentSin - updateB * currentCos);
420  currentCos = tempCos1;
421 
423  // load re[i+1], im[i+1]
425  realLo = *pInLo;
426  imLo = *(pInLo+1);
427 
429  // load re[(n/2)-1-i], im[(n/2)-1-i]
431  realHi = *pInHi;
432  imHi = *(pInHi+1);
433 
435  // calculate:
436  // realDiff = re[i+1]-re[(n/2)-1-i]
437  // realSum = re[i+1]+re[(n/2)-1-i]
439  realDiff = realLo-realHi;
440  realSum = realLo+realHi;
441 
443  // calculate:
444  // imDiff = im[i+1]-im[(n/2)-1-i]
445  // imSum = im[i+1]+im[(n/2)-1-i]
447  imDiff = imLo-imHi;
448  imSum = imLo+imHi;
449 
451  // calculate:
452  //
453  // realResultLo =
454  // re[i+1]+re[(n/2)-1-i] +
455  // (im[i+1]+im[(n/2)-1-i]) * cos( (i+1) * 2pi / n ) -
456  // (re[i+1]-re[(n/2)-1-i]) * sin( (i+1) * 2pi / n )
457  //
458  // imResultLo =
459  // im[i+1]-im[(n/2)-1-i] -
460  // (re[i+1]-re[(n/2)-1-i]) * cos( (i+1) * 2pi / n ) -
461  // (im[i+1]+im[(n/2)-1-i]) * sin( (i+1) * 2pi / n )
462  //
464 
465  realResultLo = realSum + (imSum*currentCos) - (realDiff*currentSin);
466  imResultLo = imDiff - (realDiff * currentCos) - (imSum*currentSin);
467 
469  // calculate:
470  //
471  // realResultHi =
472  // re[(n/2)-1-i]+re[i+1] +
473  // (im[(n/2)-1-i]+im[i+1]) * cos( ((n/2)-i-1) * 2pi / n ) -
474  // (re[(n/2)-1-i]-re[i+1]) * sin( ((n/2)-i-1) * 2pi / n )
475  //
476  // imResultHi =
477  // im[(n/2)-1-i]-im[i+1] -
478  // (re[(n/2)-1-i]-re[i+1]) * cos( ((n/2)-i-1) * 2pi / n ) -
479  // (im[(n/2)-1-i]+im[i+1]) * sin( ((n/2)-i-1) * 2pi / n )
480  //
481  // taking advantage of the following:
482  //
483  // sin( (i+1) * 2pi / n ) = sin ( ((n/2)-i-1) * 2pi / n )
484  // cos( (i+1) * 2pi / n ) = -cos ( ((n/2)-i-1) * 2pi / n )
485  // re[(n/2)-1-i]-re[i+1] = -(re[i+1]-re[(n/2)-1-i])
486  // re[(n/2)-1-i]-re[i+1] = -(re[i+1]-re[(n/2)-1-i])
488 
489  realResultHi = realSum - (imSum*currentCos) + (realDiff*currentSin);
490  imResultHi = -imDiff - (realDiff * currentCos) - (imSum*currentSin);
491 
493  // store results, advance low pointer forward to next complex element,
494  // and high pointer backward to previous complex element
496 
497  *pInLo++ = realResultLo/2;
498  *pInLo++ = imResultLo/2;
499  *(pInHi+1) = imResultHi/2;
500  *pInHi = realResultHi/2;
501 
502  pInHi -= 2;
503  }
504  }
505 
506  return result;
507 }
508 
510 // scalar implementation of altivec inverse real fft above
512 static int32 fft_real_inverse_scalar(float *data, int32 len)
513 {
514  int32 result = 0;
515  double updateA, updateB;
516 
517  double currentCos, currentSin, tempCos1;
518 
519  float realLo, realHi, imLo, imHi;
520 
521  float realResultLo, realResultHi, imResultLo, imResultHi;
522 
523  float realDiff, imDiff, realSum, imSum;
524 
525  float *pInLo, *pInHi;
526 
527  int32 i;
528 
530  // for length of 0 or 1 we do nothing
532  if (len < 2) return 0;
533 
535  // Given c = cos(w) and s = sin(w), if we want to find the cos and
536  // sin of w plus some small angle d, then we can do so by defining:
537  //
538  // a = 2 * ((sin(d/2)) ^ 2)
539  // b = sin(d)
540  //
541  // Then, we can calculate the cos and sin of the updated angle w+d
542  // as:
543  //
544  // cos(w+d) = c - ac - bs
545  // sin(w+d) = s - as + bc
546  //
547  // We will need to incrementally calculate cos(w) and sin(w), so we
548  // define the following scalar values. We use scalar because we
549  // need the precision of doubles, and vectors are floats.
551 
552  updateA = sin(PI/len);
553  updateB = sin(2*PI/len);
554  updateA *= updateA*2;
555 
557  // start with sin(0) and cos(0)
559 
560  currentCos = 1;
561  currentSin = 0;
562 
564  // load re[0] and im[0]. Only re[0] is stored -- im[0] is
565  // understood to be 0.
567  realLo = data[0];
568  imLo = 0;
569 
571  // load re[n/2] and im[n/2].
572  // Only re[n/2] is stored -- im[n/2] is understood to be 0.
574  realHi = data[1];
575  imHi = 0;
576 
578  // calculat sum and difference of real & imaginary values
580 
581  realDiff = realLo-realHi;
582  realSum = realLo+realHi;
583 
584  imDiff = imLo-imHi;
585  imSum = imLo+imHi;
586 
588  // calculate re[0], and im[0]. we don't bother to do the sin, cos
589  // multiplies, because we know that they are zero and one.
591 
592  realResultLo = realSum - imSum;
593  imResultLo = imDiff + realDiff;
594 
595  data[0] = realResultLo/2;
596  data[1] = imResultLo/2;
597 
599  // Start our source pointers to point at re[1] and re[(n/2)-1].
601  pInLo = &data[2];
602  pInHi = &data[len-2];
603 
605  // for each loop iteration, we calculate two complex results (four
606  // floats), so we iterate through the loop len/4 times
608  for (i = 0; i < len/4; i++) {
610  // calculate the new sin and cos values
612  tempCos1 = currentCos - (updateA*currentCos + updateB * currentSin);
613  currentSin = currentSin - (updateA*currentSin - updateB * currentCos);
614  currentCos = tempCos1;
615 
617  // load re[i+1], im[i+1]
619  realLo = *pInLo;
620  imLo = *(pInLo+1);
621 
623  // load re[(n/2)-1-i], im[(n/2)-1-i]
625  realHi = *pInHi;
626  imHi = *(pInHi+1);
627 
629  // calculate:
630  // realDiff = re[i+1]-re[(n/2)-1-i]
631  // realSum = re[i+1]+re[(n/2)-1-i]
633  realDiff = realLo-realHi;
634  realSum = realLo+realHi;
635 
637  // calculate:
638  // imDiff = im[i+1]-im[(n/2)-1-i]
639  // imSum = im[i+1]+im[(n/2)-1-i]
641  imDiff = imLo-imHi;
642  imSum = imLo+imHi;
643 
645  // calculate:
646  //
647  // realResultLo =
648  // re[i+1]+re[(n/2)-1-i] -
649  // (im[i+1]+im[(n/2)-1-i]) * cos( (i+1) * 2pi / n ) -
650  // (re[i+1]-re[(n/2)-1-i]) * sin( (i+1) * 2pi / n )
651  //
652  // imResultLo =
653  // im[i+1]-im[(n/2)-1-i] +
654  // (re[i+1]-re[(n/2)-1-i]) * cos( (i+1) * 2pi / n ) -
655  // (im[i+1]+im[(n/2)-1-i]) * sin( (i+1) * 2pi / n )
656  //
658  realResultLo = realSum - (imSum*currentCos) - (realDiff*currentSin);
659  imResultLo = imDiff + (realDiff * currentCos) - (imSum*currentSin);
660 
662  // calculate:
663  //
664  // realResultHi =
665  // re[(n/2)-1-i]+re[i+1] -
666  // (im[(n/2)-1-i]+im[i+1]) * cos( ((n/2)-i-1) * 2pi / n ) -
667  // (re[(n/2)-1-i]-re[i+1]) * sin( ((n/2)-i-1) * 2pi / n )
668  //
669  // imResultHi =
670  // im[(n/2)-1-i]-im[i+1] +
671  // (re[(n/2)-1-i]-re[i+1]) * cos( ((n/2)-i-1) * 2pi / n ) -
672  // (im[(n/2)-1-i]+im[i+1]) * sin( ((n/2)-i-1) * 2pi / n )
673  //
674  // taking advantage of the following:
675  //
676  // sin( (i+1) * 2pi / n ) = sin ( ((n/2)-i-1) * 2pi / n )
677  // cos( (i+1) * 2pi / n ) = -cos ( ((n/2)-i-1) * 2pi / n )
678  // re[(n/2)-1-i]-re[i+1] = -(re[i+1]-re[(n/2)-1-i])
679  // re[(n/2)-1-i]-re[i+1] = -(re[i+1]-re[(n/2)-1-i])
681 
682  realResultHi = realSum + (imSum*currentCos) + (realDiff*currentSin);
683  imResultHi = -imDiff + (realDiff * currentCos) - (imSum*currentSin);
684 
686  // store results, advance low pointer forward to next complex
687  // element, and high pointer backward to previous complex element
689 
690  *pInLo++ = realResultLo/2;
691  *pInLo++ = imResultLo/2;
692  *(pInHi+1) = imResultHi/2;
693  *pInHi = realResultHi/2;
694 
695  pInHi -= 2;
696  }
697 
699  // perform an inverse complex fft on the data. The resulting data
700  // is the real-only inverse fft.
702  result = FFTComplex(data, len/2, 1);
703 
704  return result;
705 }

708 // FFTRealForward
709 //
710 // Performs a real forward FFT on the data. A wrapper function for
711 // the scalar and AltiVec versions of the forward real FFT, since
712 // there is a minimum length for the AltiVec implementation.
714 int32 FFTRealForward(float *data, int32 len)
715 {
716  return fft_real_forward_scalar(data, len);
717 }
718 
720 // FFTRealInverse
721 //
722 // Performs a real inverse FFT on the data. A wrapper function for
723 // the scalar and AltiVec versions of the inverse real FFT, since
724 // there is a minimum length for the AltiVec implementation.
726 int32 FFTRealInverse(float *data, int32 len)
727 {
728  return fft_real_inverse_scalar(data, len);
729 }
